Defining Semi-Intentional Murder and the Hanafi Internal Dispute
Defines shibh al-amd and presents intra-Hanafi disagreement on its scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of shibh al-amd, distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from the Sahibayn's view, and apply the correct classification to a scenario based on the instrument used.

Core Idea
Shibh al-amd is defined by the instrument: Abu Hanifa requires sharpness; Sahibayn consider lethality.

This passage clarifies a crucial intra-Hanafi dispute on the boundaries of intentional murder (amd), semi-intentional murder (shibh al-amd), and accidental murder (khata). The classification hinges on the nature of the instrument used to strike. Abu Hanifa relies on a hadith restricting qisas to sword-like sharp weapons, while the Sahibayn consider whether the instrument typically causes death. Understanding this disagreement is essential for correctly applying diyah or qisas in homicide cases.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Recognize that the dispute concerns an intentional strike that causes death. The question is whether the act is classified as amd (intentional murder), shibh al-amd (semi-intentional), or khata (accidental).
2
Identify the instrument category
Determine whether the instrument is sharp (like a sword), heavy and typically lethal (like a large stone), or light and rarely lethal (like a small stick).
3
Apply Abu Hanifa's rule
According to Abu Hanifa, only a sharp instrument (weapon or equivalent) can constitute amd. Any non-sharp instrument, even if heavy and lethal, makes the act khata (accidental). Shibh al-amd for him is striking with an object that is neither a weapon nor equivalent, but he treats that also as khata in this passage.
Abu Hanifa's source: hadith 'La qawada illa bil-sayf' (No qisas except with a sword).
4
Apply the Sahibayn's rule
The Sahibayn classify the act based on typical lethality: if the instrument generally causes death (e.g., a large stone), it is amd. If it rarely kills (e.g., a small stick), it is shibh al-amd. They thus create a distinct intermediate category.
The Sahibayn also cite the hadith of the Jewish man killed with a stone as evidence.
5
Determine the practical difference
For a strike with a heavy stone, Abu Hanifa rules khata (diyah only), while the Sahibayn rule amd (qisas possible). For a light stick, both may classify as shibh al-amd, but Abu Hanifa may call it khata.
Later Hanafi fatwa often follows the Sahibayn for heavy lethal objects.

Source Text

[2496] (3) And shibh al-amd according to Imam Abu Hanifa is that he strikes intentionally with something that is not a weapon and not equivalent to a weapon. And the two (Sahibayn) said: if he strikes a person with a large stone or a large piece of wood, that is intentional murder. And shibh al-amd is to strike intentionally with something that generally does not kill a person. Above, by the mursal hadith, it was proved that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, for intentional murder it is necessary to strike with a sharp thing. Therefore, if he strikes intentionally with something that is not sharp, not a weapon, or not equivalent to a weapon, then it is not intentional murder but accidental murder. And there is no qisas but rather diyah is wajib. For example, if he strikes with a large stone, it is accidental murder because it is not sharp. But if it is sharp, then it is considered equivalent to a weapon and is intentional murder. The hadith has passed: from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir that the Messenger of Allah said: 'No qisas except with a sword.' (c) (Ibn Majah, chapter on no qisas except with sword, p. 384 no. 2667; al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Hudud wa al-Diyat, vol. 3 p. 84 no. 3150) And the Sahibayn say: any large thing that generally causes death, if he strikes intentionally with it, it is intentional murder. And he strikes with that thing... Footnote: (continued from previous page) A man asked: O Messenger of Allah, which sin is greatest before Allah? He said: That you call upon a rival to Allah while He created you. He said: Then which? He said: Then that you kill your child for fear that he will eat with you. (a) O you who have believed, prescribed for you is qisas concerning the killed: free for free, slave for slave, female for female. (b) Whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell... (c) He said: No qisas except with a sword.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage defines semi-intentional murder (shibh al-amd) and further clarifies the intra-Hanafi dispute on classification of homicidal acts. Abu Hanifa defines shibh al-amd as intentional striking with an object that is neither a weapon nor equivalent to a weapon. In his view, if the object is not sharp (e.g., a blunt heavy stone), the act does not qualify as intentional murder but rather as accidental (khata), requiring only diyah. The Sahibayn, however, distinguish between objects: striking with a large stone or heavy wood that ordinarily kills is intentional murder (amd), while striking with an object that rarely kills is shibh al-amd. Thus, for the Sahibayn, shibh al-amd is a separate intermediate category. The passage then repeats the hadith proof from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir that qisas is only with a sword, which Abu Hanifa uses to limit intentional murder to sharp instruments. The Sahibayn still maintain that any large lethal object suffices. The footnote adds a hadith on major sins and repeats the key Quranic verses. This passage underscores how the definition of shibh al-amd is intertwined with the broader disagreement on the instrument of murder.

Key Terms
شبه عمد (shibh al-amd): Semi-intentional murder: intentional striking with an object not typically lethal, resulting in diyah rather than qisas.
دية (diyah): Blood money, compensation paid by the killer's family for homicide that does not warrant qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does Abu Hanifa classify a blow with a large blunt stone that causes death?
A) Intentional murder (amd)
B) Semi-intentional murder (shibh al-amd)
C) Accidental murder (khata)
D) No homicide

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of homicide hinges on the instrument's nature, with Abu Hanifa requiring sharpness and the Sahibayn focusing on lethality; the mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn for heavy lethal objects.

Definition of Shibh al-'Amd and Its Rulings
Intra-Hanafi dispute on definition and shared ruling of shibh al-'amd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the definitions of shibh al-'amd according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain the shared ruling on sin, kaffarah, and diyah.

Core Idea
Shibh al-'amd: intentional but with a non-lethal tool; no qisas, but sin, kaffarah, and heavy diyah on the 'aqilah.

In Hanafi fiqh, homicides are categorized into 'amd (intentional), shibh al-'amd (quasi-intentional), and khata' (accidental). The distinction determines whether qisas applies or only diyah. This passage presents the defining criterion of shibh al-'amd according to Abu Hanifa and contrasts it with the view of the Sahibayn, while noting their agreement on the consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions on the definition
State what constitutes shibh al-'amd according to Abu Hanifa (striking with non-weapon, not equivalent to weapon) and according to the Sahibayn (striking with something that does not usually kill). Note their disagreement on tools like large stones.
The Sahibayn consider large stones/wood as 'amd, not shibh al-'amd.
2
Locate the proof for each
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith 'No qisas except with a sword' (Ibn Majah). The Sahibayn use the prophetic practice of stoning a Jew (Bukhari) and analogy to lethal tools.
The Hanafi response interprets the stoning as 'amd because the stone was lethal.
3
Analyze the common ground
Despite the definitional difference, both agree that shibh al-'amd carries sin, kaffarah (expiation), and heavy diyah on the 'aqilah, with no qisas.
The ruling on consequences is unanimous.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider striking someone with a small stick (non-lethal tool). According to both views, this is shibh al-'amd. But if the stick is large and lethal, the Sahibayn classify it as 'amd (qisas possible), while Abu Hanifa still calls it shibh al-'amd.
The practical outcome differs: qisas vs diyah only.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi fatwa collections adopt the Sahibayn's definition for practical purposes, but the consequence ruling remains unchanged.
This illustrates how ikhtilaf within the school is resolved for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشبه العمد عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله ان يتعمد الضرب بما ليس بسلاح ولا ما اجرى مجراه وقالا رحمهما الله اذا ضربه بحجر عظيم او بخشبة عظيمة فهو عمد و شبة العمد ان يتعمَّد ضربه بما لا يقتل به غالبا. و موجب ذلك على القولين الماثم والكفارة ولا قود فيه وفيه دية مغلظة على العاقلة.
Quasi-intentional murder according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) is that he intentionally strikes with something that is not a weapon nor in the status of a weapon. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them) said: If he strikes him with a large stone or a large piece of wood, it is intentional murder; and quasi-intentional murder is that he intentionally strikes him with something that does not usually kill. And the consequence according to both views is sin and kaffarah; there is no qisas in it, and in it there is a heavy diyah upon the 'aqilah.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of shibh al-'amd (quasi-intentional murder) and its legal consequences. Imam Abu Hanifa defines shibh al-'amd as striking intentionally with a tool that is neither a weapon nor considered in the same category as a weapon—such as a small stick or a small stone—since these do not typically cause death. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ: they consider striking with a large stone or large piece of wood as intentional murder ('amd) because such tools are lethal. For them, shibh al-'amd is limited to striking with something that does not usually kill, like a small stick. Despite this difference in definition, both agree on the ruling: the perpetrator incurs sin (ithm) and must pay kaffarah (expiation by freeing a believing slave or fasting two months), and no qisas (retaliation) is imposed. Instead, the 'aqilah (the paternal male relatives of the killer) must pay a heavy diyah (blood money) over three years. This ruling distinguishes shibh al-'amd from both intentional murder (which carries qisas) and accidental murder (which carries lighter diyah).

Key Terms
شبه العمد (shibh al-'amd): Intentional striking with something that is not a weapon nor equivalent to a weapon, and which does not usually kill.
دية مغلظة (diyah mughallazah): Heavy blood money (full diyah of 100 camels) paid by the 'aqilah over three years.
عاقلة ('aqilah): The paternal male relatives (asabah) of the killer who are obliged to pay diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the defining characteristic of shibh al-'amd?
A) Striking with any non-weapon tool.
B) Striking with a tool that does not usually kill.
C) Striking with a weapon or equivalent.
D) Accidental striking.

Key Takeaway
The definition of shibh al-'amd differs between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, but they agree on the ruling: sin, kaffarah, and heavy diyah on the 'aqilah, with no qisas.

Diyat — Blood Money

Diyah for a Hand: Half the Blood Money
Ruling with proof that a hand warrants half diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a cut hand warrants half diyah and explain the proof from the hadith and the principle of substitution for qisas.

Core Idea
A cut hand warrants half of full diyah – fifty camels – because qisas cannot be exactly exacted.

This passage addresses the diyah (blood money) for amputation of a hand. When retaliation (qisas) is not possible—for example, if the hand is already severed or exact equivalence cannot be achieved—the compensation reverts to diyah. The author cites a hadith that explicitly fixes the amount at half the full diyah, i.e., fifty camels. Understanding this ruling clarifies how Hanafi law handles intentional injuries where exact retribution is infeasible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Note the act: intentional cutting of a hand. The ruling (hukm) is that half diyah is wajib (obligatory). The text opens with 'عليه نصف الدية' – upon it is half the diyah.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because diyah is a financial obligation established by zanni (probable) proof.
2
Locate the first proof: the athar from Ibrahim
Ibrahim al-Nakha'i states that for any intentional wound where qisas cannot be carried out, the compensation is from the offender's own wealth, not from the 'aqilah. This establishes the principle that when qisas is impossible, diyah becomes due.
This athar is cited from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Locate the second proof: the hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb
The hadith lists various body parts and their diyah. For the hand, it explicitly says: 'وفي اليد اذا قطعت نصف العقل' – and for the hand if cut, half the 'aql (diyah). This directly gives the amount.
The hadith is reported in Sunan Abi Dawud and Sunan al-Nasa'i.
4
Understand the explicit wording
The phrase 'نصف العقل' (half the 'aql) means half of the full diyah. Full diyah is 100 camels (or equivalent), so half is 50 camels. The ruling is clear and unambiguous.
'Aql' is another term for diyah in this context.
5
Note the authority level
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, the core Hanafi texts, and is accepted by all schools (muttafaq alayh). The hadith provides qati' (definitive) indication, though its transmission is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
Since the ruling is agreed upon, no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنايات عليه نصف الدية كاٹنے کے لئے دایاں ہاتھ باقی نہیں رہا۔ اس لئے اب وہ اپنے ہاتھ کے لئے دیت لے گا۔ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ قصاص کے لئے کچھ نہ ہو تو دیت لے گا۔ عن ابراهیم قال ما كان من جرح من العمد لا يستطاع فيه القصاص فهو على الجارح في ماله دون عاقلته ( الف ) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۰۱ العمد الذي لا يستطاع فيه القصاص ج خامس میں ۲۰۳ نمبر ۲۷۴۰۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہاں قصاص لینا ممکن نہیں وہاں دیت لازم ہے۔ اور ایک ہاتھ کے لئے پوری جان کی آدھی دیت ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عمر بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده ... وقضى رسول الله لل الله في الانف اذا جدع الدية كاملة وان جدعت ثندؤته فنصف العقل خمسون من الابل او عدلها من الذهب او الورق او مائة بقرة او الف شلة وفي اليد اذا قطعت نصف العقل وفي الرجل نصف العقل (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب دیات الاعضاء ص ۲۷۸ نمبر ۴۵۶۴ رنسائی شریف ، ذکر حدیث عمرو بن حزم في العقول و اختلاف الناقلین لرص ۶۶۸ نمبر ۴۸۵۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک ہاتھ کے لئے آدھی دیت یعنی پچاس اونٹ ہے۔
The book of injuries: upon it is half the diyah. Because for cutting, the right hand remained not. So now he will take the diyah for his hand. Previously it passed that when there is nothing for qisas, he takes diyah. From Ibrahim: He said, 'Whatever intentional wound for which qisas cannot be carried out, it is upon the one who inflicted the wound from his own wealth, not from his 'aqilah.' From this athar it became known that where qisas is not possible, diyah is obligatory. And for one hand, half the diyah of a full life is due. For this there is this hadith: From 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather... The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) ruled that for the nose if it is cut off, full diyah; and if its tip is cut, half the 'aql: fifty camels or their equivalent in gold or silver or one hundred cows or one thousand sheep; and for the hand if cut, half the 'aql; and for the foot, half the 'aql. From this hadith it became known that for one hand half diyah, i.e., fifty camels.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the diyah for a hand. The matn states: 'عليه نصف الدية' (upon it is half the diyah). The commentary explains this ruling, noting that when qisas is not possible (e.g., the hand is already cut off or retaliation cannot be exactly applied), then diyah (blood money) becomes obligatory. The text cites two proofs: First, an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a tabi'i) that any intentional wound where qisas cannot be exacted is compensated from the offender's own wealth, not from the 'aqilah. Second, a hadith from the Prophet (ﷺ) reported by 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb, specifying that for a cut hand, half the 'aql (i.e., half of full diyah) is due, which is fifty camels. The hadith also lists other organs. Thus, the Hanafi position is clear: a hand commands half diyah.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide or bodily harm
عاقلہ ('aqilah): The clan or group of male relatives who are jointly liable for paying diyah in cases of accidental killing or injury
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional homicide or bodily harm

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full diyah (100 camels)
B) Half diyah (50 camels)
C) One-third diyah
D) One-tenth diyah

Key Takeaway
For an intentional cut of a hand where qisas is impossible, the Hanafi ruling imposes half diyah (fifty camels) from the offender's own wealth.

Diyat — Blood Money
beginner

Definition and Evidence for Diyat (Blood Money)
Defines diyat and provides Quranic and hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define diyah according to the Hanafi school and state the primary Quranic and hadith evidence for its obligation.

Core Idea
Diyah is a wajib monetary compensation for unintentional and quasi-intentional homicide and injuries, proven by Quran and Sunnah.

The Book of Diyat begins with a precise definition: diyah is the financial penalty imposed in cases where killing or injury is not purely intentional. Understanding this concept and its scriptural basis is fundamental to Islamic criminal law. This lesson unpacks the definition and the strong textual evidence that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Legal Category
Recognize that diyah applies specifically to unintentional (khata) and quasi-intentional (shibh amd) homicide and unintentional injuries. It is not imposed for pure intentional homicide (where qisas applies).
2
Note the Definition and Scope
The author defines diyah as a monetary penalty (جرمانه) that becomes obligatory (لازم) in the mentioned cases. This sets the scope for the entire book.
3
Locate the Quranic Evidence
The verse from Surah al-Nisa (4:92-93) explicitly mentions 'diyah musallamah' (delivered blood money) for accidental killing, establishing the obligation.
The verse also mentions other components like freeing a slave and fasting alternatives.
4
Examine the Hadith Evidence
The hadith from the Prophet's letter to the people of Yemen, transmitted by Amr ibn Hazm, details the specific amounts of diyah for various body parts and injuries. This provides the Sunnah basis for the quantities.
The hadith is a key source for the values (e.g., 100 camels for full diyah, 5 camels for a tooth).
5
Recognize the Hanafi Position's Strength
Both the Quran (qat'i al-thubut) and the hadith (though mursal, it is accepted in this context) provide strong evidence. The Hanafi school relies on these texts to classify diyah as wajib (obligatory) in these cases.
The obligation is financial (gharamah) and falls on the asaba (tribal group) in unintentional cases, as per Hanafi law.

Book of Blood Money. In cases of quasi-intentional homicide, unintentional homicide, unintentional wounding, etc., the monetary penalty that becomes obligatory is called diyah. Its evidence is this verse: 'It is not for a believer to kill a believer except by mistake. And whoever kills a believer by mistake, then the freeing of a believing slave and a blood money delivered to his family, unless they remit...' (Quran 4:92-93). This verse proves several types of diyat. (2) This hadith mentions many diyat: 'The Messenger of Allah wrote to the people of Yemen a letter containing the obligations, the Sunnas, and the blood monies...' [then the hadith text explaining amounts of diyat for various body parts]. (End of page).
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Diyat (Blood Money) by defining the term. Diyah is the monetary compensation imposed in cases of homicide that are not purely intentional, or in unintentional injuries. The author then provides the primary evidence from the Quran (Surah al-Nisa, 4:92-93). The verse outlines the consequences of accidental killing: freeing a believing slave and paying diyah to the victim's family, with variations depending on the status of the victim and the relationship of the killer's community. The passage also references a lengthy hadith from the letter of the Prophet to the people of Yemen, transmitted by 'Amr ibn Hazm, which details the amounts of diyah for different body parts and injuries. This hadith is a key source for the specific values of diyat in Islamic law. The Hanafi school relies on these texts to establish the obligatory amounts and categories of diyah.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Monetary compensation for homicide or injury in cases other than pure intentional killing, as defined by the author.
قتل خطأ (qatl khata): Unintentional killing, where the killer did not intend to kill.
قتل شبہ عمد (qatl shibh amd): Quasi-intentional killing, such as hitting with a small object not likely to kill.

Key Takeaway
Diyah is wajib compensation for unintentional homicide and injuries, established by Quran and hadith, with specific amounts detailed in the Sunnah.

Definition of Diyah and Its Quranic Proof
Defines diyah and provides Quranic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define diyah and identify its primary Quranic evidence (4:92-93).

Core Idea
Diyah is a financial penalty for homicide/injury, established by Quran 4:92-93 for unintentional killing.

Before we examine the detailed rulings of diyat (blood-money), we must understand what diyah is and where its obligation comes from. This lesson introduces the definition of diyah and its foundational proof from the Quran, specifically verses 92-93 of Surah al-Nisa'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the term 'diyah' in the text and note that it is defined as a financial penalty (mal se jo jurmana) that becomes obligatory (lazim).
The definition is given in Urdu: 'مروری نوں قتل شبہ عمد میں قتل خطاء، زخم خطاء وغیرہ ہونے پر مال سے جو جرمانہ لازم ہوتا ہے اس کو دیت کہتے ہیں۔'
2
Extract the scope of diyah
The text specifies that diyah applies to qatl shibh 'amd (near-intentional killing), qatl khata' (accidental killing), and wound khata' (accidental injury). Note that intentional killing (amd) is not included here.
This scope distinguishes diyah from qisas, which applies to intentional killing.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
The text states 'its proof is this verse' and quotes Quran 4:92-93. Identify the exact verses and note that they address unintentional killing.
The verse number appears reversed in the OCR: (الف) ( آیت ۹۳٫۹۲ سورۃ النساء). The correct order is 92-93.
4
Analyze the proof structure
The verse explicitly commands payment of diyah (ودية مسلمة الى اهله) for accidental killing. It also mentions exceptions and expiation (kaffarah). This establishes diyah as a primary obligation.
The verse also mentions freeing a slave or fasting, which are expiatory acts, not part of diyah itself.
5
Note the types of diyah indicated
The passage notes 'many types of diyah are proven' from the verse. The verse itself distinguishes between the victim's community: if from believers, if from hostile people, if from treaty people. This leads to variations in diyah amount and liability.
This will be expanded in later lessons on diyah categories.

مروری نوں قتل شبہ عمد میں قتل خطاء، زخم خطاء وغیرہ ہونے پر مال سے جو جرمانہ لازم ہوتا ہے اس کو دیت کہتے ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ وما كان لمؤمن ان يقتل مؤمنا الاخطاء ومن قتل مؤمنا خطاء فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة ودية مسلمة الى اهله الا ان يصدقوا فان كان من قوم عدولكم وهو مؤمن فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة وان كان من قوم بينكم وبينهم ميثاق فدية مسلمة الى اهله وتحرير رقبة مؤمنة فمن لم يجد فصيام شهرين متتابعين توبة من الله وكان الله عليما حكيما . ومن يقتل مؤمنا متعمدا فجزاءه جهنم خالدا فيها وغضب الله عليه ولعنه واعد له عذابا عظيما (الف) ( آیت ۹۳٫۹۲ سورۃ النساء (۴) اس آیت سے کئی قسم کی دیات کا ثبوت ہے
Regarding the meaning: the penalty that becomes obligatory from wealth upon the occurrence of qatl shibh 'amd, qatl khata', wound khata', etc. is called diyah. Its proof is this verse: 'And it is not for a believer to kill a believer except by mistake. And whoever kills a believer by mistake must free a believing slave and pay blood-money to his family unless they remit it...' [4:92-93]. From this verse, many types of diyah are proven.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Diyat by defining diyah as a financial penalty imposed for criminal acts such as qatl shibh 'amd, qatl khata', and injuries caused by mistake. The author then provides the primary textual evidence from the Quran, Surah al-Nisa' verses 92-93, which establishes diyah for unintentional killing. The verse also mentions the expiation of freeing a slave or fasting. The author notes that this verse proves multiple types of diyah.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Financial compensation obligatory for homicide or injury, especially in cases of unintentional killing or near-intentional (shibh 'amd) and accidental killing.
قتل شبہ عمد (qatl shibh 'amd): Near-intentional killing: the killer intended to strike but not to kill. In Hanafi law, this incurs diyah, not qisas.
قتل خطاء (qatl khata'): Accidental killing: the killer had no intent to harm. This incurs diyah and kaffarah.

Diyah is a financial penalty for unintentional homicide and injury, proven by Quran 4:92-93, and is distinct from qisas.

Diyat — Blood Money

Diyah Amounts from the Hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm
Quotes the Prophetic letter detailing diyah for various injuries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the standard diyah amounts for life, paired organs, single organs, specific wounds, fingers, and teeth as derived from the hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet's letter fixed diyah at 100 camels for life and specified clear amounts for each injury.

The diyah (blood money) system is a cornerstone of Islamic criminal law, providing financial compensation for homicide and bodily harm. This lesson anchors you in the primary textual source—the famous letter of the Prophet to the people of Yemen carried by 'Amr ibn Hazm. Memorizing these amounts is essential for any student of Hanafi fiqh, as they form the basis for all subsequent rulings on diyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the authoritative source
Recognize that this hadith is a written document from the Prophet himself, making it a primary legislative text for diyah rules.
The letter was sent to several Yemeni leaders and tribes.
2
Memorize the base diyah for taking a life
The full diyah for a free person is 100 camels. This is the foundation for all proportional amounts.
Hanafi school uses this as the standard; alternative payments in gold/silver are also accepted.
3
Categorize injuries by type
The hadith distinguishes between paired organs (both eyes, lips, testicles, etc.) which carry full diyah, and single organs (one eye, one hand, one foot) which carry half diyah. Head wounds are separately categorized: ma'mumah (to brain) and ja'ifah (penetrating body cavity) each one-third diyah; munqilah (bone-displacing) 15 camels; mudihah (exposing bone) 5 camels.
Also includes fingers (10 camels each) and teeth (5 camels each).
4
Memorize the specific numbers
Create a mental table: full diyah = 100 camels; half diyah = 50 camels; one-third = 33.33 camels (or 33 + 1/3); munqilah = 15; mudihah = 5; per finger = 10; per tooth = 5.
In practice, equivalent values in gold (1000 dinars) or silver may be used.
5
Note the qisas principle
The hadith also affirms qisas for intentional killing and that a man is killed for killing a woman (gender equality in qisas, though diyah differs).
This is consistent with Hanafi law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) اس حدیث میں بہت سی دیتوں کا تذکرہ ہے۔ ان رسول الله الله كتب الى اهل اليمن كتابا فيه الفرائض والسنن والديات وبعث به مع عمرو بن حزم فقرئت على اهل اليمن هذه نسختها من محمد النبي الى شرحبيل بن عبد كلال ونعيم بن عبد كلال والحارث بن عبد كلال قيل ذي رعين ومعافر وهمدان اما بعد! وكان في كتابه ان من اعتبط مؤمنا قتلا عن بينة فانه قود الا ان يرضى اولياء المقتول وان في النفس الدية مائة من الابل والانف اذا اوعب جدعه الدية وفى اللسان الدية وفى الشفتين الدية وفى البيضتين وفي الذكر الدية وفي الصلب الدية وفى العينين الدية وفى الرجل الواحدة نصف الدية وفى المامومة ثلث الدية وفي الجائفة ثلث الدية وفي المنقلة خمس عشرة من الابل وفي كل اصبع من اصابع اليد والرجل عشر من الابل وفي السن خمس من الابل وفي الموضحة خمس من الابل وان الرجل يقتل بالمرأة وعلى اهل الذهب الف دينار، وفي رواية وفى العين الواحدة نصف الدية وفي اليد الواحدة نصف الدية وفى الرجل الواحدة نصف الدية
(2) This hadith mentions many diyahs. The Messenger of Allah (صلى الله عليه وسلم) wrote to the people of Yemen a letter containing the obligations, practices, and diyahs, and sent it with 'Amr ibn Hazm. It was recited to the people of Yemen. Its copy: From Muhammad the Prophet to Shurahbil ibn 'Abd Kalaal, Nu'aym ibn 'Abd Kalaal, and al-Harith ibn 'Abd Kalaal, and to the people of Dhi Ra'ayn, Ma'afir, and Hamdan. To proceed: Indeed, whoever intentionally kills a believer with clear evidence, then execution (qisas) is required unless the heirs of the slain forgive. And for the life, the diyah is one hundred camels. And for the nose when completely cut off, full diyah. And for the tongue, full diyah. And for the lips, full diyah. And for the testicles, diyah. And for the penis, diyah. And for the spine, diyah. And for both eyes, diyah. And for one foot, half diyah. And for the ma'mumah (skull wound), one-third diyah. And for the ja'ifah (penetrating wound), one-third diyah. And for the munqilah (displacing bone), fifteen camels. And for each finger of the hand or foot, ten camels. And for a tooth, five camels. And for the mudihah (cut to bone), five camels. And a man is killed for a woman (i.e., qisas applies). And for the people of gold, one thousand dinars. And in another narration: And for one eye, half diyah; and for one hand, half diyah; and for one foot, half diyah.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage presents the famous hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm, a written document from the Prophet to the Yemeni leaders, detailing the diyah amounts for various injuries and homicides. It establishes the standard diyah for a life as 100 camels, and then specifies amounts for body parts: full diyah for paired organs (eyes, lips, testicles, etc.) and half diyah for single ones (one foot, one hand, etc.). It also mentions diyah for head wounds (ma'mumah, ja'ifah, munqilah) and for fingers and teeth. The hadith includes the principle that a man is killed for a woman (qisas). It also mentions an alternative payment in gold (1000 dinars). This hadith is a primary source for the details of diyah in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Financial compensation for homicide or injury, as specified in the hadith.
نفس (nafs): Life; here referring to the diyah for the life of a free person: 100 camels.
مأمومة (ma'mumah): A wound reaching the brain (skull fracture into the head). Doses: one-third of full diyah.
جائفة (ja'ifah): A wound penetrating the body cavity (abdomen or chest). Doses: one-third diyah.
منقلة (munqilah): A wound that displaces a bone. Doses: fifteen camels.
موضحة (mudihah): A wound that cuts to the bone, exposing it. Doses: five camels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 5 camels
B) 10 camels
C) 15 camels
D) 20 camels

Key Takeaway
The hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm provides the definitive diyah amounts for life, organs, and wounds, serving as the foundation for Hanafi diyat law.

Ruling on Qatl Shibh 'Amd: Diyah Mughallazah and Kaffarah
States the ruling for near-intentional killing and its proofs from Quran and hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for shibh 'amd (diyah mughallazah on the aqila and kaffarah on the killer) and cite the proofs from Quran 4:92 and the hadith of Abu Hurayra.

Core Idea
Shibh 'amd incurs stern diyah on the aqila and kaffarah, not qisas.

The Hanafi school distinguishes three categories of homicide: intentional ('amd), near-intentional (shibh 'amd), and accidental (khata'). This passage focuses on shibh 'amd — a killing done intentionally but without a sharp weapon. The ruling is that the killer's male agnatic relatives (aqila) must pay a stern diyah (diyah mughallazah), and the killer must also perform an expiation (kaffarah). The proofs are drawn from the Quranic verse on accidental killing (4:92) by analogy, and from the Prophetic ruling in the hadith of the two women from Hudhayl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act is qatl shibh 'amd: killing with intention but without a sharp weapon. The Hanafi school treats this as a distinct category between 'amd and khata'.
Sharp weapon typically means a knife, sword, or anything that cuts. A club, stone, or fist is not sharp.
2
State the ruling
Two obligations arise: (1) diyah mughallazah on the aqila (stern compensation payable by the killer's male relatives), and (2) kaffarah on the killer (expiation: freeing a slave or fasting two months).
The diyah is 'mughallazah' meaning heavier; details of taghliz follow in the next passage.
3
Locate the primary proof
The author cites Quran 4:92: 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake must free a believing slave and pay diyah to his family...' Although the verse literally addresses khata', shibh 'amd is analogized to it because both lack the use of a sharp weapon (the illa is the absence of a sharp tool).
In Hanafi usul, qiyas is applied: khata' (asl) has diyah and kaffarah; shibh 'amd (far') shares the same 'illa (no sharp instrument) and thus receives the same obligations, but with taghliz due to the intentional component.
4
Trace the secondary proof (hadith)
The hadith of Abu Hurayra: two women from Hudhayl fought; one struck the other with a non-sharp object causing death. The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) ruled that the diyah is on the aqila. This concrete case establishes that shibh 'amd incurs diyah on the aqila, not qisas.
The hadith is found in Bukhari and Muslim. It demonstrates the practical application of the ruling.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dimension
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may not recognize shibh 'amd as a distinct category; they might classify all intentional killing as 'amd requiring qisas. The Hanafi school maintains the intermediate category, affecting the type of compensation.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is whether the killer faces qisas or diyah. In Hanafi law, shibh 'amd is non-qisas.

۲۳۳۷۱) (۱) اگر کسی نے کسی آدمی کو شبہ عمد میں قتل کر دیا تو اس کے عاقلہ پر دیت مغلظہ ہے اور اس پر کفارہ ہے۔ کسی نے کسی آدمی کو دھاردار ہتھیار کے علاوہ سے جان بوجھ کر قتل کر دیا جس کو شبہ عمد کہتے ہیں اس کی وجہ سے قاتل کے خاندان پر دیت مغلظہ لازم ہوگی اور خود قاتل پر کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ آیت میں ہے۔ ومن قتل مؤمنا خطاء فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة ودية مسلمة الى اهله ( الف ) ( آیت ۹۲ سورۃ النساء۴) قتل شبه عمد قتل خطا کے درجے میں ہے اس لئے آیت سے پتا چلا کہ دیت لازم ہوگی اور غلام آزاد کرنا ہوگا (۲) اور خاندان پر دبیت لازم ہو ۔ کیا دلیل حدیث کا ٹکڑا ہے۔ ان ابا هريرة انه قال اقتصلت امرأتان من هزيل ... وقضى ان دية المرأة على عاقلتها (ب) ( بخارى شریف، باب جنين المرأة وان العقل على والد و عصبة الوالد لاعلی الولد ص ۱۰۲۰ نمبر ۶۹۱۰ مسلم شریف، باب دیتہ الجنين ووجوب الدية في قتل الخطاء وشبه العمد على عاقلتہ الجانی ص ۶۲ نمبر ۱۶۸۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ت نے جان کر بغیر دہہ ردار چیز سے دوسری عورت کو مارا تھا تو مقتل شبه عمد ہوا اور اس کی دیت قاتلہ کے خاندان پر لازم کی ۔ اور ۔۔ مغلظہ کی تفصیل آگے ہے۔
23371) (1) If a man kills a man in shibh 'amd, then on his aqila is a stern (mughallazah) diyah, and on him is kaffarah. If someone kills a man intentionally but not with a sharp weapon, which is called shibh 'amd, due to this the killer's family is required to pay stern diyah, and the killer himself must perform kaffarah. In the verse is: 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake must free a believing slave and pay diyah to his family...' (4:92). Qatl shibh 'amd is in the category of qatl khata', so from the verse it is understood that diyah is necessary and freeing a slave. And the family is required to pay diyah. What is the proof? A piece of hadith: Abu Hurayra said: 'Two women from Hudhayl fought... and he ruled that the diyah of the woman is on her aqila.' (Bukhari and Muslim). From this hadith it is understood that one woman intentionally hit the other with something not sharp, so it was qatl shibh 'amd, and the diyah was imposed on the killer's family. And the details of taghliz will follow.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage lays down the ruling for qatl shibh 'amd (near-intentional killing): it requires a stern diyah (mughallazah) payable by the killer's aqila (agnatic relatives) and an expiation (kaffarah) on the killer himself. The author explains that shibh 'amd is killing with intention but without a sharp weapon. The proof is drawn from the Quranic verse 4:92, which deals with killing by mistake. The Hanafi school places shibh 'amd in the same category as khata' for the obligation of diyah, though the diyah is mughallazah (stern) in severity. Additionally, the hadith of Abu Hurayra about two women from Hudhayl is cited: one struck the other with something not sharp, causing death, and the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) ruled that the diyah is on the aqila. This illustrates that shibh 'amd incurs diyah on the aqila, not qisas. The verse and hadith together establish the obligation.

Key Terms
شبه عمد (shibh 'amd): Near-intentional killing: killing intentionally but without a sharp weapon, resulting in diyah mughallazah on the aqila.
دية مغلظة (diyah mughallazah): Stern diyah: a heavier compensation, payable in specific higher-quality camels.
عاقلة (aqila): The male agnate relatives (asabah) of the killer who collectively pay the diyah in cases of khata' and shibh 'amd.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation: for shibh 'amd, freeing a believing slave or fasting two consecutive months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qisas and diyah
B) Diyah mughallazah on the aqila and kaffarah on the killer
C) Only diyah on the killer
D) Kaffarah only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, shibh 'amd (intentional killing without a sharp weapon) incurs a stern diyah payable by the aqila and a personal kaffarah, not qisas.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Diyah for Shibh 'Amd: 100 Camels in Four Categories
Ruling with proof for shibh 'amd diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah amount for shibh 'amd according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, identify the four camel categories, and explain when taghliz applies.

Core Idea
Shibh 'amd diyah: 100 camels in four equal categories; taghliz only in camels, not gold or silver.

This passage from Sharh al-Sameri specifies the diyah (blood money) for shibh 'amd (near-intentional killing) according to the Hanafi school. It details the exact number and ages of camels, and clarifies that the severity (taghliz) of the diyah only applies when payment is made in camels, not in gold or silver. The proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states the diyah for shibh 'amd according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Note that it is 100 camels, not a different number.
2
Break down the four categories
The 100 camels are equally divided into four age categories: bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqah, jadha'ah. Each category has 25 camels.
3
Understand taghliz (severity)
Taghliz means the diyah is more severe, achieved by paying higher-quality (older) camels. It only applies when diyah is paid in camels, not in gold or silver.
If diyah is paid in gold/silver, it is the standard amount (1000 dinars or 10000 dirhams) without taghliz.
4
Analyze the dalil
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud explicitly lists the four categories, confirming the breakdown. This is a sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its indication is clear (qati al-dalala).
The hadith is quoted in the passage: 'Abdullah said: In shibh 'amd, twenty-five hiqqah, twenty-five jadha'ah, twenty-five bint labun, twenty-five bint makhad.'
5
Note the intra-Hanafi context
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The passage does not mention Imam Muhammad's view, but the mufta bihi is the 100-camel breakdown.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۳۳۸ (۲) اور شبہ عمد کی دیت امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک سو اونٹ ہیں چار طرح کے۔ چھپیس بنت مخاض ، پچھپیس بنت لبون بچیں حقہ اور پچیس جذعہ۔ اور تغلیظ نہیں ثابت ہوگی مگر صرف اونٹ میں ۔ پس اگر اونٹ کے علاوہ کی دیت کا فیصلہ کیا تو مغلظہ نہیں ہوگی۔ قتل شبہ عمد اور قتل خطاء میں ہر حال میں ایک ہزار دینار یا دس ہزار درہم ہیں۔ اس لئے اگر دینار اور درہم دیت دے تو ان میں تغلیظ نہیں ہو سکتی صرف اونٹ کی دیت میں تغلیظ ہوگی وہ تعداد میں تو ہمیشہ سو اونٹ ہی لازم ہوں گے۔ البتہ عمر کے اعتبار سے اعلی اونٹ لازم کرے تو تغلیظ ہوگی اور ادنی اونٹ لازم کرے تو تخفیف ہو جائے گی۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ قال عبد الله في شبه العمد خمس وعشرون حقة وخمس وعشرون جذعة وخمس وعشرون بنات ليون وخمس وعشرون بنات مخاض (ج) ( ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی دیتہ الخطاء شبه العمد ص ۲۷۷ نمبر (۴۵۵۳) اس حدیث میں اونٹ کی تفصیل ہے۔
2338 (2) And the diyah of shibh 'amd according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them) is one hundred camels of four types: twenty-five bint makhad, twenty-five bint labun, twenty-five hiqqah, and twenty-five jadha'ah. And taghliz (sternness) is only established in camels. So if a ruling is given for diyah other than camels, then it is not mughallazah. In qatl shibh 'amd and qatl khata', in any case, [the diyah] is one thousand dinars or ten thousand dirhams. Therefore, if one gives diyah in gold or silver, there is no taghliz in them; taghliz only occurs in the diyah of camels. As for the number, it is always one hundred camels that are obligatory. However, in terms of age, if one gives higher-quality camels, it is taghliz, and giving lower-quality camels reduces (lighter). The proof of this is the hadith: 'Abdullah said: In shibh 'amd, twenty-five hiqqah, twenty-five jadha'ah, twenty-five bint labun, and twenty-five bint makhad.' (Abu Dawud). This hadith details the camels.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage details the diyah amount for qatl shibh 'amd according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: 100 camels of four age categories (bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqah, jadha'ah). The taghliz (severity) of the diyah only applies when paying in camels; if paid in gold or silver, it is the standard amount (1000 dinars/10000 dirhams) without taghliz. Taghliz means the camels must be of a higher age (and thus value), while lower age reduces the penalty. The hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud confirms the four categories. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
شبه عمد (shibh 'amd): Near-intentional killing; diyah is 100 camels in four categories.
تغليظ (taghliz): Sternness or severity in diyah, achieved by paying in higher-quality camels.
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A female camel in its second year.
بنت لبون (bint labun): A female camel in its third year.
حقة (hiqqah): A female camel in its fourth year.
جذعة (jadha'ah): A female camel in its fifth year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi diyah for shibh 'amd is 100 camels in four equal categories, with taghliz applicable only when payment is in camels.

Diyah Maghallazah in Shibh Amd: Liability and Composition
Ruling with proof for shibh amd diyah and kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of shibh amd, identify who is liable for diyah and kaffarah, and explain the composition of the aggravated diyah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Shibh amd diyah is on the aqilah — 100 camels in four equal categories — and kaffarah on the killer.

Having understood the basic categories of homicide in Hanafi fiqh, you now encounter the distinct ruling for shibh amd (quasi-intentional killing). This passage from the Book of Diyat establishes that the diyah (blood money) in shibh amd is aggravated and falls on the killer's aqilah, while the killer must also perform kaffarah. The author provides Quranic and hadith proofs, then details the composition of the aggravated diyah according to the dominant Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act (shibh amd) and what is the hukm? The act is killing intentionally but without a sharp weapon. The ruling: diyah maghallazah on aqilah and kaffarah on the killer.
Shibh amd is between amd (full intent, qisas) and khata' (mistake, diyah without aggravation).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 4:92 (on khata') and the hadith of the two women from Hudhayl. Why is the verse on khata' used for shibh amd? Because shibh amd is analogized to khata' in lacking a sharp weapon, so the same rule applies.
Thubut and dalala are both zanni for the hadith, but the Quranic verse is qat'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse makes diyah wajib on the aqilah in khata'. The hadith explicitly applies that to shibh amd by placing the diyah on the aqilah of the woman who struck another without a sharp weapon. This establishes the ruling.
The imperative (diyah) indicates wujub; the placement on aqilah specifies liability.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, Imam Muhammad differs on the exact composition of the 100 camels. The text gives the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: equal quarters of bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqah, and jadha'ah. Imam Muhammad (and al-Shafi'i) have a different distribution.
The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf per Al-Marghinani.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, the diyah is equal age categories; under Imam Muhammad, more older camels are required. Taghliz only applies to camel diyah; if paid in gold/silver, no taghliz.
Taghliz means requiring higher-quality (older) camels.

حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) موضحہ زخم میں پانچ اونٹ ہیں۔ اور مرو قتل کیا جائے گا عورت کے بدلے میں۔ اور سونے والے پر ہزار دینار ہے (الف) کسی نے مومن کو قتل کیا غلطی سے تو مومن غلام کو آزاد کرنا ہے اور دیت اس کے وارث کو سپرد کرتا ہے (ب) ابو ہریرڈ نے فرما یا بیل کی دو عورتوں نے قتال کیا فیصلہ کیا کہ عورت کی دیت اس کے خاندان پر ہے (ج) حضرت عبداللہ نے فرمایا قتل شبه عمد میں چھپیں حقہ پچیس جذعہ، چیپس بنت لبون اور پچیس بنت مخاض ہیں۔
If a man kills a man in quasi-intentional killing, then upon his aqilah is an aggravated diyah, and upon him is kaffarah. (1) If someone kills a person in quasi-intentional killing, then upon his aqilah is an aggravated diyah, and upon him is kaffarah. The verse: 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake, then freeing a believing slave and a diyah delivered to his family' (Surah an-Nisa 4:92). Quasi-intentional killing is in the category of mistaken killing, so from the verse it becomes clear that diyah is obligatory and freeing a slave is obligatory. And upon the family, diyah is obligatory. Evidence: a piece of hadith: Abu Hurairah said: Two women from Hudhayl fought... and he judged that the diyah of the woman is upon her aqilah. From this hadith it is known that she deliberately killed the other woman with something other than a sharp weapon, so it was quasi-intentional killing, and its diyah was imposed on the killer's family. The detail of taghliz comes later. (2) The diyah of quasi-intentional killing according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is one hundred camels in four quarters: twenty-five bint makhad, twenty-five bint labun, twenty-five hiqqah, and twenty-five jadha'ah. And taghliz is only established with camels. So if judgment is given with diyah from other than camels, it is not aggravated. In quasi-intentional and mistaken killing, in all cases it is one thousand dinars or ten thousand dirhams. Therefore, if he gives diyah in dinars or dirhams, taghliz cannot occur; taghliz only applies to camel diyah in terms of age: if he imposes high-quality camels, it is taghliz; if low-quality, it is takhfif. Its evidence: Abdullah said regarding quasi-intentional killing: twenty-five hiqqah, twenty-five jadha'ah, twenty-five bint labun, twenty-five bint makhad. (c) In this hadith is the detail of camels. Footnote: (From previous page) For a wound exposing bone, five camels. And the killer will be killed in exchange for a woman. And for the sleeping person, one thousand dinars. (a) Whoever kills a believer by mistake must free a believing slave and hand over the diyah to his heirs. (b) Abu Hurairah said: Two women fought, and he judged that the diyah of the woman is upon her family. (c) Abdullah said: in quasi-intentional killing, twenty-five hiqqah, twenty-five jadha'ah, twenty-five bint labun, and twenty-five bint makhad.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Book of Diyat. The author states the ruling that in shibh amd (quasi-intentional killing), the diyah is maghallazah (aggravated) and is upon the aqilah (the killer's clan), and the killer must also pay kaffarah (expiation). The proof is derived from the verse on mistaken killing (Quran 4:92) because shibh amd is analogous to khata' (mistake) in that it does not involve a sharp weapon, so the same rule applies. Additional proof is from the hadith of the two women from Hudhayl where the Prophet (peace be upon him) placed the diyah on the aqilah. The author then explains the composition of the diyah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: 100 camels divided equally into four categories based on age: bint makhad (1-2 years), bint labun (2-3), hiqqah (3-4), and jadha'ah (4-5). Taghliz (aggravation) only applies when the diyah is paid in camels; if paid in gold or silver, the amount is fixed (1000 dinars or 10000 dirhams) and no aggravation occurs. Aggravation is achieved by requiring camels of high age, while concession is by allowing lower age. The footnotes clarify related points: the diyah for a wound that exposes bone is five camels, and accidental killing requires freeing a slave. The hadith of Abdullah provides the same four categories. This lesson is a memorization anchor for the diyah of shibh amd.

Key Terms
شبه عمد (shibh amd): Killing intentionally but with something other than a sharp weapon, not reaching the level of amd (full intent).
دية مغلظة (diyah maghallazah): Aggravated blood money: 100 camels with specific age requirements, higher value.
عاقلة (‘aqilah): The group of agnate relatives (asabah) of the killer who are liable to pay diyah in cases of khata' and shibh amd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Shibh amd requires diyah maghallazah on the aqilah (100 camels in four equal categories) and kaffarah on the killer, based on Quranic analogy and hadith.

Diyah Composition for Shibh Amd: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Taghliz
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyah composition for shibh amd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf) on the composition of diyah for shibh amd, contrast it with the position of Imam Muhammad, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
The diyah for shibh amd is 100 camels in four equal quarters, but Imam Muhammad adds 40 pregnant camels for taghliz.

This passage examines an important intra-Hanafi difference: the exact composition of the camel diyah for quasi-intentional killing (shibh amd). While Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the diyah consists of 25 camels each of four age categories, Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) and Imam al-Shafi'i argue for a more aggravated composition including pregnant camels. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate conflicting evidence within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Identify the ruling as presented in the text: the diyah for shibh amd is 100 camels divided equally into four types: 25 bint makhad, 25 bint labun, 25 hiqqah, 25 jadha'ah.
The text mentions 'twenty-six' but this is likely an OCR error; the correct number is 25.
2
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view
Note that Imam Muhammad (a major Hanafi authority) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold a different composition: 40 pregnant jadha'ah (khalifah), 30 hiqqah, 30 bint labun.
This view is based on the practice of Uthman and Zayd ibn Thabit.
3
Examine the evidence for each view
Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf rely on the hadith of Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) narrated in Abu Dawud. The opposing view relies on the practice of Uthman and Zayd, also recorded by Abu Dawud.
The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Abdullah is stronger in transmission and directly from the Prophet.
4
Understand the concept of taghliz
Taghliz (aggravation) in diyah applies only to camels, not to gold or silver. In shibh amd, if paid in camels, the composition itself constitutes taghliz; if paid in dinars/dirhams, the amount is fixed without taghliz.
The ages of the camels also affect taghliz: higher age (e.g., jadha'ah) is more severe.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under the majority Hanafi view, the diyah is four equal quarters; under Imam Muhammad's view, it is more aggravated with 40 pregnant camels. This affects the actual camels to be paid.
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Commentary
This passage begins a dispute map regarding the composition of the diyah for shibh amd (quasi-intentional killing). The author first presents the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the diyah is 100 camels divided equally into four categories: 25 bint makhad (1-2 years), 25 bint labun (2-3), 25 hiqqah (3-4), and 25 jadha'ah (4-5). Taghliz (aggravation) only applies to camel diyah, meaning if the diyah is paid in gold or silver, the amount is fixed (1000 dinars/10000 dirhams) without taghliz. The proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (or similar) specifying these four types. Then the commentary introduces the opposing view of Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani, a Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i. Their position is based on the practice of Uthman and Zayd ibn Thabit: the maghallazah diyah consists of 40 pregnant jadha'ah (khalifah), 30 hiqqah, and 30 bint labun. The author clarifies the camel age terminology: bint makhad (year 2), bint labun (year 3), hiqqah (year 4), jadha'ah (year 5), and after 5 years it is thaniyya or mutli (adult). The dispute centers on whether taghliz is achieved by specific types and proportions. The mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as supported by the hadith of Abdullah. The author then continues with the definition of camel ages, which is essential for understanding the composition.

Key Terms
تغليظ (taghliz): Aggravation of the diyah by requiring camels of higher age (e.g., jadha'ah instead of bint makhad) or specific numbers/types.
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A female camel in its second year (one year old).
جذع (jadha'ah): A male or female camel in its fifth year (four years old).
بنت لبون (bint labun): A female camel in its third year (two years old).
حقة (hiqqah): A female camel in its fourth year (three years old).
خلفة (khalifah): A pregnant camel.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi diyah for shibh amd consists of 100 camels in four equal age categories according to the majority view, with taghliz only applying to camel diyah.

Aqilah Liability in Accidental Killing and Its Exceptions
Ruling with proof for accidental killing and exceptions to aqilah liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that diyah for accidental killing is on the aqilah, identify the four exceptions (amd, slave, sulh, i'tiraf), and apply the rule to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Aqilah pays diyah for khata' and shibh amd, but not for amd, slaves, sulh, or confession.

In accidental killing, the diyah is not on the killer alone but on his extended family (aqilah). However, this transfer of liability has clear boundaries. This lesson explains the basic rule from the Quran and Sunnah and the four cases where the aqilah is exempt, based on the athar of Umar.

Guided Path
1
State the rule for accidental killing
What is the ruling on diyah in qatl khata'? Who pays it?
The rule: diyah on aqilah, kaffarah on killer.
2
Locate the primary proofs
Identify the hadith of Jabir (Sunnah) and the athar of Umar that support this rule.
Hadith: Prophet placed diyah on aqilah. Athar: Umar listed four exceptions.
3
Understand the principle behind aqilah liability
Why is the aqilah liable? Because they should have prevented the killing. This applies when the diyah is directly from the killing, not from a contract.
The diyah must be 'directly obligatory' on the killer to transfer to aqilah.
4
List the four exceptions
Name the cases where aqilah is not liable: intentional killing (amd), killing of a slave, settlement (sulh), and confession (i'tiraf).
In these cases, the obligation arises from the killer's own act of contract or confession, not from the killing itself.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a scenario, decide if aqilah is liable or not.
For example: If the killer settles with the heirs for 100 camels, aqilah is not liable.

حاشیہ : (الف) زید بن ثابت نے فرمایا مغلظہ میں چالیس جذعہ خلفہ ہیں اور تمیں حقہ ہین اور تمیں بنت لبون ہیں ( ب ) حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا قتل عمد میں اور غلام کے قتل میں اور صلح میں اور جرم کے اقرار کر لینے میں خاندان والے دیت نہیں دیں گے۔
(3) And in accidental killing, the diyah is obligatory on the aqilah and kaffarah on... [The commentary says:] The verse regarding diyah and kaffarah has already passed. The principle of diyah being obligatory on aqilah is that whatever diyah is directly obligatory on the killer is obligatory on his family, like the diyah of accidental killing is directly obligatory on the killer, so it is on his family. Similarly, the diyah of shibh amd is directly obligatory on the killer, so it is on the killer's family because they did not prevent him from killing. (2) In the hadith: Jabir ibn Abdullah said: Two women from Hudhayl, one killed the other, and each had a husband and children. He said the Prophet made the diyah of the killed woman on the aqilah of the killer. From this hadith it is known that in accidental killing, the diyah is on the killer's aqilah. In intentional killing, qisas is obligatory on the killer, not diyah; rather if sulh (settlement) is made in place of qisas with diyah or property, then it becomes obligatory. Therefore, it is not on the killer's aqilah. Similarly, if sulh is made for accidental killing with property, or if he confesses to property, then the property is obligatory due to his confession or sulh, so it is not on his family. Similarly, if diyah is obligatory on a slave, it is not on his family but his master pays it. In this athar: Umar said: 'Intentional killing, slave, sulh, and confession are not upon the aqilah.' From this athar it is known that intentional killing, sulh property, confession property, and property obligatory on a slave are not on the aqilah.
Footnote: (a) Zayd ibn Thabit said: In the maghallazah, there are forty jadha'ah khalifah, thirty hiqqah, and thirty bint labun. (b) Umar said: In intentional killing, killing of a slave, sulh, and confession of crime, the family does not pay diyah.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for accidental killing (khata'). The author states the ruling that in khata', diyah is upon the aqilah and kaffarah is upon the killer. The proof is from the verse (Quran 4:92) already cited, and the hadith of the two women from Hudhayl (via Jabir). The commentary then explains the general principle: any diyah that is directly on the killer becomes on his aqilah because they should have restrained him. This applies to khata' and shibh amd. However, there are exceptions: 1) Intentional killing (amd): the penalty is qisas, not diyah, so aqilah is not liable unless the heirs forego qisas in exchange for diyah; but even then, that diyah is on the killer, not aqilah, because it is a contractual sulh. 2) If the killer settles (sulh) with the heirs for property or confesses to a debt, that obligation is on him alone, not on aqilah. 3) Diyah for killing a slave: the aqilah of the slave's killer is not liable; the master pays, or the killer pays from his own wealth. Evidence is the athar of Umar: 'Intentional killing, slave, sulh, and confession are not on the aqilah.' Thus, aqilah liability is limited to khata' and shibh amd when the diyah is directly due for the killing itself, not when it results from settlement or confession. The footnotes clarify that the taghliz composition (from Uthman and Zayd) is for shibh amd, and Umar's ruling is on exceptions.

Key Terms
قتل خطأ (qatl khata'): Accidental killing, e.g., unintentionally shooting someone while hunting.
صلح (sulh): Settlement between the killer and the heirs by paying diyah or property to avoid qisas.
اعتراف (i'tiraf): Confession of the killer that he owes diyah, making it a debt on him alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases does the aqilah NOT have to pay the diyah?
A) Accidental killing (khata')
B) Quasi-intentional killing (shibh amd)
C) Intentional killing where the heirs accept sulh (settlement)
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
Aqilah is liable for diyah in accidental and quasi-intentional killings, but not when the obligation arises from a settlement, confession, intentional killing, or killing of a slave.

Diyat — Blood Money

Aggravation of Diyat and Liability of the 'Aqila for Accidental Killing
Explains tathliz and 'aqila liability for qatl al-khata'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on aggravation of diyat (tathliz) and identify the parties liable for diyat in accidental killing (qatl al-khata'), including exceptions.

Core Idea
Aggravation of diyat applies only to camels; for accidental killing, the 'aqila pays diyat, not the killer.

This passage from the Book of Diyat establishes two key rulings: first, the aggravation (tathliz) of diyat by requiring higher-aged camels applies exclusively when diyat is paid in camels; second, for accidental killing, the financial liability (diyat) falls on the 'aqila (the killer's clan), while the expiation (kaffarah) remains on the killer personally. The text also delineates exceptions where the 'aqila is not liable, such as intentional killing, slave victims, and cases of settlement or acknowledgment by the killer.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on tathliz
Identify that aggravation of diyat (requiring higher-age camels) applies only when diyat is paid in camels. If diyat is adjudged from other property (e.g., gold, silver), there is no aggravation.
The footnote (a) from Zayd ibn Thabit specifies the composition of aggravated diyat: 40 jadha'ah khalifah, 30 hiqqah, 30 bint labun.
2
Identify the evidence for tathliz
The statement 'ولا يثبت التغليظ الا فى الابل خاصة' is the direct textual ruling. It is supported by the footnote (a) showing the composition, which implies the aggravation is camel-specific.
3
State the ruling on diyat for accidental killing
The passage states: 'وفي قتل الخطأ تجب به الدية على العاقلة والكفارة على القاتل.' Thus, diyat is wajib upon the 'aqila; kaffarah is on the killer personally.
The 'aqila are the paternal relatives (asaba) excluding the killer.
4
Examine the proof for 'aqila liability
The hadith of Jabir ibn 'Abdullah (Abu Dawud, Bukhari) directly shows the Prophet placing diyat on the 'aqila of the killer. This is the primary dalil. An athar from 'Umar also lists exceptions.
The hadith establishes the general rule; the athar clarifies exceptions.
5
List the exceptions to 'aqila liability
The passage and the athar mention: intentional killing (qatl al-'amd), killing of a slave, cases where the killer settles or acknowledges liability, and where the killer confesses. In these, the 'aqila is not liable; the killer pays personally (or master pays for slave).
The rationale is that the 'aqila's liability is based on negligence; these cases involve deliberate action or personal acknowledgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخمس وعشرون جذعة ولا يثبت التغليظ الا فى الابل خاصة فان قضى بالدية من غير الابل لم تتغلظ ( ۲۳۳۹] (۳) وفي قتل الخطأ تجب به الدية على العاقلة والكفارة على القاتل. دیت اور کفارہ کے بارے میں اوپر آیت گزر چکی ہے۔ عاقلہ پر دیت لازم ہونے کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جودیت براہ راست قاتل پر لازم ہو وہ اس کے خاندان پر لازم ہوتی ہے جیسے قتل خطا کی دیت براہ راست قاتل پر لازم ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے یہ اس کے خاندان پر لازم ہوگی قتل شبہ عمد کی دیت بھی براہ راست قاتل پر لازم ہوتی ہے اس لئے وہ بھی قاتل کے خاندان پر لازم ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ انہوں نے قاتل کو قتل سے روکا نہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله ان امرأتين من هذيل قتلت احداهما الاخرى ولكل واحدة منهما زوج وولد ، قال فجعل النبي لدية المقتولة على عاقلة القاتلة (ابوداؤد شریف، باب دیۃ الجنین ، ص ۲۷۷، نمبر ۴۵۷۵/ بخاری شریف، باب جنین المرأة وان العقل على الوالد و عصبة الوالد الخ ہیں ۱۰۲۰ نمبر ۶۹۰۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قتل خطاء میں دیت قاتل کے عاقلہ پر ہے۔ قتل عمد میں قاتل پر قصاص لازم ہوتا ہے دیت لازم نہیں ہوتی ہے بلکہ بعد میں قصاص کے بدلے دیت اور مال پر صلح کرلے تو لازم ہوگی ۔ اس لئے یہ قاتل کے عاقلہ اور خاندان پر لازم نہیں ہوگی۔ اسی طرح قتل خطا کے بدلے کسی مال پر صلح کر لے یا کسی مال کا اعتراف کرے تو یہ قاتل کے اعتراف کرنے یا صلح کرنے کی وجہ سے مال لازم ہوا اس لئے اس کے خاندان پر لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اسی طرح غلام پر دیست لازم ہو تو وہ اس کے خاندان پر لازم نہیں ہوگی بلکہ اس کا آقا ادا کرے گا۔ اس اثر میں ہے۔ عن عمر قال العمد والعبد والصلح والاعتراف لا يعقل العاقلة (ب) (سن ليبقى ، باب من قال لاتقتل العاقلة عمدا ولا عبدا ولاصلحا ولا اعترافاج نامن ص ۱۸۱ نمبر ۱۶۳۵۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ قتل عمد ، مال صالح ، مال اعتراف اور غلام پر لازم ہونے والا مال عاقلہ پر لازم نہیں ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) زید بن ثابت نے فرمایا مغلظہ میں چالیس جذعہ خلفہ ہیں اور تمیں حقہ ہین اور تمیں بنت لبون ہیں ( ب ) حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا قتل عمد میں اور غلام کے قتل میں اور صلح میں اور جرم کے اقرار کر لینے میں خاندان والے دیت نہیں دیں گے۔
(It says:) Twenty-five jadha'ah, and aggravation is only established specifically for camels. So if diyat is adjudged from other than camels, it is not aggravated. (Point 3) In accidental killing, diyat is obligatory upon the 'aqila (family/clan) and expiation upon the killer. ... The rule regarding diyat being binding upon the 'aqila is that whatever diyat is directly binding on the killer becomes binding on his family, like the diyat for accidental killing. Similarly, diyat for quasi-intentional killing is also binding on the killer's family because they did not prevent the killer. There is a hadith from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah about two women from Hudhayl, one killed the other, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) placed the diyat on the 'aqila of the killer. This shows diyat for accidental killing is on the 'aqila. For intentional killing, qisas is obligatory, not diyat, unless they settle for diyat or property after qisas, then it becomes binding but not on the 'aqila. Similarly, if reconciliation or acknowledgment occurs, it is due to the killer's action, not on the 'aqila. Also, diyat on a slave is not on the 'aqila but on the master. There is an athar from 'Umar: 'Intentional killing, a slave, reconciliation, and acknowledgment — the 'aqila does not pay.' Footnotes: (a) Zayd ibn Thabit said: In the aggravated (diyat), forty jadha'ah khalifah, thirty hiqqah, and thirty bint labun. (b) 'Umar said: In intentional killing, a slave, reconciliation, or acknowledgment, the family does not pay diyat.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from the Book of Diyat. First, the rule of tathliz (aggravation) of diyat: the additional burden (i.e., the higher age of camels in the case of aggravated diyat) applies only when the diyat is paid in camels. If the diyat is paid in other forms (like gold or silver), the aggravation does not apply. This is indicated by the phrase "وخمس وعشرون جذعة ولا يثبت التغليظ الا فى الابل خاصة" (twenty-five jadha'ah, and aggravation is only for camels). The footnote (a) from Zayd ibn Thabit confirms the composition of the aggravated diyat: forty jadha'ah khalifah (pregnant camels), thirty hiqqah, and thirty bint labun. Second, the ruling for accidental killing (qatl al-khata'): the diyat is obligatory upon the 'aqila (the killer's tribe or clan), while the kaffarah (expiation) is upon the killer personally. The 'aqila includes the paternal relatives who would normally inherit, excluding the killer. The rationale is that they should have prevented the killer from being careless. The passage then lists exceptions where the 'aqila is not liable: intentional killing (where qisas applies), settlement or acknowledgment by the killer (since it becomes a personal debt), and cases where a slave is killed (the master pays, not the 'aqila). These exceptions are proven by a hadith from Jabir and an athar from 'Umar. The footnote (b) gives the wording of 'Umar's ruling.

Key Terms
تغليظ (tathliz): Aggravation of diyat by requiring camels of higher age categories (e.g., jadha'ah) in certain types of killing.
عاقلة ('āqila): The group of paternal relatives (tribe or clan) of the killer who are responsible for paying diyat in cases of accidental killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In accidental killing (qatl al-khata'), who is liable to pay the diyat according to the Hanafi school?
A) The killer personally
B) The 'aqila (paternal relatives) of the killer
C) The state treasury (bayt al-mal)
D) The victim's family

Key Takeaway
In accidental killing, the diyat is paid by the 'aqila, not the killer, and aggravation of diyat applies only when paid in camels.

The Exact Composition of Diyat for Accidental Killing: 100 Camels in Five Categories
Specifies the exact composition of diyat for accidental killing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact number and categories of camels required for diyat in accidental killing, and explain the Hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Diyat for accidental killing is 100 camels divided equally into five specific age categories, proven by the Hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.

In this lesson, we examine the precise composition of the diyat (blood money) for accidental killing according to the Hanafi school. The text specifies that the diyat consists of 100 camels, divided into five categories of 20 each, based on the age and gender of the camels. The ruling is firmly grounded in a hadith narrated by Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). Understanding this exact composition is essential for correctly calculating and applying the diyat in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Context
The passage states that the diyat for accidental killing is 100 camels, divided into fifths (akhmas). Note that this ruling applies specifically to accidental killing (qatl al-khata'), not intentional killing.
2
List the Five Categories
The five categories are: bint makhad (female 2nd year), ibn makhad (male 2nd year), bint labun (female 3rd year), hiqqah (female 4th year), and jadha'ah (female 5th year). Each contributes 20 camels.
The hadith clarifies that ibn makhad is male.
3
Understand the Age Definitions
Review the key terms: each category refers to a specific age milestone. For example, bint makhad has completed one year and entered the second; jadha'ah has completed four years and entered the fifth.
After five years, the camel is called thani or muthanna.
4
Examine the Hadith Proof
The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud (quoted in Sunan Abi Dawud and Sunan al-Nasa'i) explicitly enumerates the five categories with 'twenty' each. This is the primary textual evidence for the Hanafi position.
The Arabic text is given: 'عشرون حقة وعشرون جذعة...'
5
Confirm Cross-Madhhab Consistency and Differences
All four Sunni schools agree on the total of 100 camels, but they differ on the distribution of ages. The Hanafi school's five categories are specific and based on this hadith.
Shafi'i and Maliki schools have different age distributions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدية في الخطأ مائة من الابل اخماسا عشرون بنت مخاض وعشرون ابن مخاض وعشرون بنت لبون وعشرون حقة وعشرون جذعة [۱۳۳۲۰ (۴) قتل خطا میں دیت سو اونٹ ہیں پانچ طرح کے۔ میں بنت مخاض اور میں ابن مخاض اور میں بنت لبون اور میں حقہ اور میں جذع حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن مسعود قال قال رسول الله الله الله في دية الخطاء عشرون حقة وعشرون جذعة وعشرون بنت مخاض وعشرون بنت لبون وعشرون بنى مخاض ذكر (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الدیہ کم ھی؟ ص ۲۷۷ نمبر ۴۵۴۵ رنسائی شریف ذکر استان دیتہ الخطاء ص ۶۶۲ نمبر ۴۸۰۶) اس حدیث سے قتل خطا میں اونٹ کی تعداد کا پتا چلا۔
And the diyat for accidental killing is one hundred camels in fifths: twenty bint makhad, twenty ibn makhad, twenty bint labun, twenty hiqqah, and twenty jadha'ah. [13,320 (4)] In accidental killing, the diyat is one hundred camels of five types: twenty bint makhad, twenty ibn makhad, twenty bint labun, twenty hiqqah, and twenty jadha'ah. There is a hadith: From 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said concerning the diyat for accidental killing: 'Twenty hiqqah, twenty jadha'ah, twenty bint makhad, twenty bint labun, and twenty ibn makhad (male).' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Kitab al-Diyat, Bab al-Diyat Kam Hiya, no. 4545; Sunan al-Nasa'i, no. 4806). This hadith clarifies the number of camels for accidental killing.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage provides the exact composition of the diyat for accidental killing (qatl al-khata'). According to the Hanafi school, the diyat is 100 camels, divided into five equal categories: 20 bint makhad (female camel in second year), 20 ibn makhad (male camel in second year), 20 bint labun (female camel in third year), 20 hiqqah (female camel in fourth year), and 20 jadha'ah (female camel in fifth year). This division is known as 'akhmās' (in fifths). The commentator explains the ages of each category: ibn makhad is a camel that has completed one year and entered the second; bint labun is in the third year; hiqqah in the fourth; jadha'ah in the fifth; after five years it is called 'thanī' or 'muthannā' (a camel whose milk tooth has fallen and two new teeth have appeared). The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) which the author quotes. Note that the hadith includes twenty ibn makhad (male), while the initial statement listed 'ibn makhad' without specifying gender; the hadith clarifies it is male. This ruling is consistent with the established practice from the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Key Terms
بنت مخاض (bint makhāḍ): A female camel that has entered its second year (completed one year).
ابن مخاض (ibn makhāḍ): A male camel that has entered its second year.
بنت لبون (bint labūn): A female camel that has entered its third year.
حقّة (ḥiqqah): A female camel that has entered its fourth year.
جذعة (jadha'ah): A female camel that has entered its fifth year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) 100 of one type

Key Takeaway
The diyat for accidental killing is precisely 100 camels divided into five age categories, as established by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.
