Diyah for Ammah (Ma'mumah) Wound: One-Third of Full Blood Money
Fixed diyah for ammah which reaches the brain membrane

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah amount for an ammah wound and identify its proof from the hadith of Amr bin Hazm and Amr bin Shu'ayb.

Core Idea
A wound reaching the brain membrane incurs one-third of full diyah.

Wounds to the head are categorized by severity, and the ammah (or ma'mumah) is a serious wound that penetrates the skull and reaches the brain membrane. Islamic law fixes its blood money at one-third of the full diyah. In this lesson, we examine the evidence from the Sunnah and the precise amount owed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wound and its ruling
Recognize that ammah (ma'mumah) is a wound reaching the brain membrane. The diyah is one-third of full diyah.
Full diyah = 100 camels, so 33.33 camels or equivalent.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Find the two hadiths: the letter of Amr bin Hazm and the narration of Amr bin Shu'ayb (Abu Dawud, Nasa'i).
Both explicitly state 'one-third'.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'one-third' is explicit (dalala qati'a) in assigning the fraction, leaving no room for ijtihad.
Thubut is zanni (ahad hadith) but the meaning is clear.
4
Note the equivalent amounts
The diyah can be paid in camels, gold (dinars), silver (dirhams), cattle, or sheep as per the hadith.
Hanafi mufta bihi: 33.33 camels or equivalent in currency.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage gives the diyah for ammah (also called ma'mumah), a wound that breaks the bone and reaches the brain membrane (the thin covering of the brain). The diyah is one-third of the full blood money, which amounts to 33.33 camels (i.e., 33 camels plus one-third of a camel), or the equivalent in gold, silver, cattle, or sheep. The proof is from two hadiths: the letter of Amr bin Hazm and the hadith of Amr bin Shu'ayb. Both explicitly state one-third. This is the Hanafi position.

Blood Money for Ja'ifah Wound
Fixed diyah for ja'ifah wound

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah amount for a ja'ifah wound and explain the ruling when it penetrates through.

Core Idea
A ja'ifah wound incurs one-third diyah; two-thirds if it goes through.

In this lesson, we examine the fixed blood money (diyah) for a wound that penetrates into the body cavity, known as ja'ifah. The ruling is based on explicit prophetic hadith and is consistent across the Hanafi school. We will also explore the extension to a through-and-through wound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is causing a ja'ifah wound. The ruling is a fixed diyah of one-third of the full blood money.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'وفي الجائفة ثلث الدية' (For ja'ifah, one-third of the blood money).
Recorded in Abu Dawud and Nasa'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit fractional assignment in the hadith directly proves the amount. The word 'ثلث' (one-third) specifies the exact proportion.
4
Distinguish the through-and-through case
If the wound penetrates through the body, it is counted as two independent ja'ifah wounds, each incurring one-third, totaling two-thirds.
The text says: 'فان نفذت فهى جائفتان ففيهما ثلثا الدية'.
5
Note the Hanafi position
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, based on clear textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۳۵۹] (۲۳) وفى الجائفة ثلث الدية فان نفذت فهى جائفتان ففيهما ثلثا الدية [۲۳۵۹] (۲۳) اور جاکفہ زخم میں دیت کی تہائی ہے۔ پس اگر آر پار ہو جائے تو وہ دو جائفے ہیں تو ان دونوں میں دیت کی دو تہائی ہے۔ جائفہ جوف سے مشتق ہے جس کا ترجمہ ہے پیٹ کے اندر تک پہنچ جاتا۔ یہاں وہ زخم مراد ہے جو پیٹ کی جانب سے یا پیٹھ کی جانب سے آنتوں تک زخم پہنچ جائے۔ اس زخم میں پوری دیت کی تہائی ہے یعنی 33.33 اونٹ یا 333.33 دینار یا 3333.33 درہم لازم ہوں گے۔ اوپر ابو داؤد شریف اور نسائی شریف کی حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ وفی الجائعة ثلث الدیۃ ( نسائی شریف ، نمبر ۴۸۵۷ را بو داؤد شریف، نمبر (۴۵۶۴
[2359] (23) And for the ja'ifah, one-third of the blood money. Then if it penetrates through, then there are two ja'ifahs, and for them two-thirds of the blood money. [2359] (23) And for a ja'ifah wound, one-third of the blood money. So if it goes through, then that is two ja'ifahs, and for both of them, two-thirds of the blood money. Ja'ifah is derived from jawf (cavity), which means reaching inside the abdomen. Here it refers to a wound that reaches the intestines from the side of the belly or back. For this wound, one-third of the full blood money is due, i.e., 33.33 camels or 333.33 dinars or 3333.33 dirhams. Above, the hadith of Abu Dawud and Nasa'i has passed: 'And for ja'ifah, one-third of the blood money.' (Nasa'i, no. 4857; Abu Dawud, no. 4564).
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage gives the diyah for ja'ifah, a wound that penetrates into the body cavity (jawf)—specifically, a wound that reaches the intestines or internal organs from the front or back. The diyah is one-third of the full blood money (33.33 camels or equivalent). If the wound goes through the body (nufadh), exiting from the other side, it is treated as two independent ja'ifah wounds, and the total diyah becomes two-thirds of the full blood money (66.66 camels). The proof is from the same hadiths of Amr bin Hazm and Amr bin Shu'ayb that also mention ma'mumah. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
جائفه (ja'ifah): A wound that penetrates into the body cavity (abdomen or chest).
جوف (jawf): The body cavity, especially the abdomen or chest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One-half of full blood money
C) Two-thirds of full blood money
D) Full blood money

Key Takeaway
The diyah for a ja'ifah wound is one-third; if it goes through, two-thirds.

Diya for Munaqqilah Wound: Amount and Proof
Ruling on diya amount for munaqqilah wound with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the diya of a munaqqilah wound (15 camels) and identify the dalil from the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm.

Core Idea
Munaqqilah wound diya: 15 camels – one-tenth plus half of one-tenth of full diya.

This lesson deals with a specific type of head wound called munaqqilah, where the bone is fractured and displaced. The Hanafi school has fixed a specific compensation (diya) for this injury, derived from the prophetic hadith. We will examine the amount, the calculation, and the textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the infliction of a munaqqilah wound. The ruling is that the perpetrator must pay a fixed diya of 15 camels.
This is a financial penalty, not a physical punishment.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm, which explicitly states 'and for the munaqqilah, fifteen camels'. This is a hadith ahad but accepted in diyat.
The hadith is recorded by Nasa'i and other collections.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit wording 'fifteen camels' is unambiguous and indicates a fixed amount. The imperative to pay is implied from the context of setting blood money.
The text is qat'i al-dalalah (clear in meaning) but zanni al-thubut (transmitted through ahad).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may have different classifications or amounts, but the Hanafi position is based on this hadith and the practice of the Caliphs.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; our focus is on the Hanafi view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The authoritative fatwa position is 15 camels or their equivalent value, as held by the Hanafi madhhab.
This is zahir al-riwayah, from the core works of Imam Muhammad.

Source Text

۲۳۵۷ (۲۱) وفى المنقلة عشر ونصف عشر الدية
اور منتقلہ زخم میں دیت کا دسواں حصہ اور دسویں حصے کا آدھا حصہ ہے۔
پوری دیت کا دسواں حصہ دس اونٹ ہوئے اور دس اونٹ کا آدھا پانچ اونٹ ہوئے تو کل پندرہ اونٹ دیت ہوئی۔

And for the munaqqilah wound, one-tenth and half of one-tenth of the diya. And in the munaqqilah wound, one-tenth of the diya and half of the tenth share. One-tenth of the full diya is ten camels, and half of ten camels is five camels, so total fifteen camels is the diya. In the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm: 'And for the ma'mumah, one-third of the diya; and for the ja'ifah, one-third of the diya; and for the munaqqilah, fifteen camels.' (Nasa'i Sharif, hadith no. 4857). Commentary
This passage states the ruling for the diya of a munaqqilah wound (a wound that displaces bone). The ruling is that the diya is one-tenth of the full diya (10 camels) plus half of one-tenth (5 camels), totaling 15 camels. The proof is from the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm, which is a well-known document on diyat. Additionally, an athar from Abd al-Razzaq confirms this amount. The commentary explains the calculation: full diya is 100 camels; one-tenth is 10; half of that is 5; sum is 15 camels. Note that the text uses 'asher wa nisf asher al-diya' meaning one-tenth and half of one-tenth of the diya. The Hanafi school relies on this hadith, which is considered mursal but accepted in matters of diyat. The authority weight is from the hadith, which is considered reliable for this ruling.

Key Terms
المنقلة (al-munaqqilah): A wound that fractures the bone and displaces it, but does not reach the cranium or the membrane; it is a type of head wound.
عشر ونصف عشر الدية (ashar wa nisf ashar al-diyah): One-tenth and half of one-tenth of the full diya (i.e., 15 out of 100 camels).

Diya for Ja'ifah Wound and Its Doubling Upon Penetration
Ruling on diya for ja'ifah wound and its doubling if it penetrates both sides

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diya for a single ja'ifah wound and for a penetrating ja'ifah wound, and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
A single ja'ifah wound carries one-third diya; if it penetrates through, it counts as two wounds with two-thirds diya.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the ja'ifah wound—a wound reaching the body cavity. The passage specifies the fixed compensation (diya) and explains how a through-and-through wound is treated as two separate wounds, each requiring its own diya. You will learn the amounts and the prophetic evidence supporting them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wound type (ja'ifah)
Read the definition: ja'ifah is a wound that penetrates into the jauf (body cavity), reaching the intestines from front or back. Distinguish it from head wounds like ma'mumah.
The etymology from 'jauf' clarifies the anatomical criterion.
2
State the diya for a single ja'ifah
The text rules: 'For the ja'ifah, one-third of the diya.' That equals 33.33 camels or equivalent in gold/silver.
This is a fixed amount, not subject to adjustment.
3
Understand the condition of penetration (nuffidh)
If the wound goes through the body (e.g., from belly to back), it is no longer a single wound. The text says: 'then if it penetrates, it is two ja'ifahs.' Each side counts as a separate wound.
Penetration means the wound exits the body, creating two distinct openings (front and back).
4
Calculate the total diya for penetrating wound
Since each ja'ifah carries one-third diya, two such wounds total two-thirds of the full diya (66.66 camels).
The total is the sum of the two fixed amounts.
5
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The ruling is based on hadith (e.g., Amr ibn Hazm and Amr ibn Shu'ayb) and an athar from Mujahid. The explicit wording 'one-third' and 'if it penetrates, two-thirds' is the direct proof.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalalah).

And for the ja'ifah wound, one-third of the diya. Then if it penetrates [both sides], it is two ja'ifahs, so in them two-thirds of the diya. And in the ja'ifah wound, one-third of the diya. So if it goes through, it becomes two ja'ifahs, so in those two, two-thirds of the diya. Ja'ifah is derived from jauf, meaning it reaches inside the belly. Here it means a wound that reaches the intestines from the belly side or the back side. In this wound, one-third of the full diya is owed: 33.33 camels or 333.33 dinars or 3333.33 dirhams. The hadith from Abu Dawud and Nasa'i has passed: 'And for the ja'ifah, one-third of the diya' (Nasa'i no. 4857, Abu Dawud no. 4564). Footnote: (a) Zaid ibn Thabit said: For the mudihah wound, five camels; for the hashimah, ten camels; for the munaqqilah, fifteen; for the ma'mumah, one-third of the full diya. (b) In the ma'mumah wound, one-third of the diya; and in the ja'ifah, one-third of the diya; and in the munaqqilah, fifteen camels. (c) In the hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb: that in the ma'mumah wound, one-third of the full diya, thirty-three and one-third camels, or its value in gold, silver, cows, or sheep. And for the ja'ifah wound, the same diya. There is an athar: from Mujahid, he said: for the ja'ifah, one-third; if it penetrates, then two-thirds (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq).

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for the ja'ifah wound (a wound that reaches the internal cavity, specifically the intestines). The single ja'ifah carries one-third of the diya (33.33 camels). If the wound penetrates through the body (nuffidh), meaning it goes from one side to the other, it is considered two separate ja'ifah wounds (one on each side), and the total diya becomes two-thirds (66.66 camels). The proof is from the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm and Amr ibn Shu'ayb, and also from an athar of Mujahid. The footnote includes statements from Zaid ibn Thabit and others, confirming the amounts for various wound types. The commentary explains the etymology of ja'ifah (from jauf, meaning cavity). The ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position in Zahir al-Riwayah. Note that the diya for ja'ifah is the same as for ma'mumah.

Key Terms
الجائفة (al-ja'ifah): A wound that penetrates into the body cavity (jauf), reaching the intestines, from the front or back.
نفذت (nuffidhat): If the wound penetrates through the body, exiting from the other side, thus constituting two separate wounds.

Diya for All Fingers of the Hand
Ruling on diya for all five fingers with or without palm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diya for all five fingers of one hand (with and without the palm) and explain the proof from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
The diya for all five fingers of one hand is half the full diya (50 camels), and cutting the palm adds nothing extra.

In Hanafi fiqh, the diya (blood money) for injuries follows specific fixed amounts. This passage addresses a common scenario: cutting all five fingers of one hand, and whether cutting the palm along with the fingers increases the compensation. The ruling is that half the full diya is due, regardless of whether the palm is included. We will examine the textual evidence and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first line: 'And for the fingers of the hand, half the diya. Then if he cuts them with the palm, then in it half the diya.' The ruling is clear: cutting all five fingers of one hand incurs half the diya, and if the palm is also cut, the amount is still half.
Half of full diya = 50 camels (full diya = 100 camels).
2
Understand the components
Each hand has five fingers. The diya per finger is 10 camels (from hadith). So for five fingers, 5 × 10 = 50 camels. This matches half the full diya.
The amounts are fixed and not subject to estimation.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'The fingers are equal, ten camels each.' This hadith (from Abu Musa) establishes equality among fingers and the specific amount. The Hanafi school relies on this as a proof for the diya of each finger.
Hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
4
Apply the palm scenario
The passage explains that the palm is considered part of the hand. Therefore, cutting the palm along with the fingers does not add extra diya beyond the 50 camels for the hand. This is supported by the athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab.
The palm's diya is included in the hand's diya.
5
Note the implication
If the cut extends beyond the palm into the forearm, additional hukuma (estimated compensation) may apply for the forearm part, as per fiqh principles not detailed here.
This lesson only covers fingers and palm.

۲۳۶۰ (۲۴) وفى اصابع اليد نصف الدية فان قطعها مع الكف ففيها نصف الدية
ہاتھ کی ساری انگلیوں میں آدھی دیت ہے۔ پس اگر اس کو تھیلی سمیت کا نا تو بھی آدھی دیت ہے۔
ہر ہاتھ میں پانچ انگلیاں ہوتی ہیں اور ہر انگلی کی دیت دس اونٹ ہے۔ اس لئے پانچ انگلیوں کی دیت پچاس اونٹ ہوئے۔ اور پچاس اونٹ ایک ہاتھ کی دیت ہے۔ اس لئے ہاتھ کی پانچ انگلیوں کی دیت پچاس اونٹ ہوئے اور پچاس اونٹ ایک ہاتھ کی دیت ہے۔ اس لئے ہاتھ کی پانچوں انگلیوں کو تھیلی سمیت کا نا تب بھی آدھی دیت لازم ہوگی۔ ہتھیلی تک ہاتھ شمار ہوتا ہے اور ہاتھ کی دیت پچاس اونٹ ہے اس لئے ہتھیلی تک کاٹے گا تب بھی پوری دیت کی آدھی یعنی پچاس اونٹ لازم ہوں گے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی موسى عن النبي الله قال الاصابع سواء عشر عشر من الابل (ب)(ابوداؤد شریف، باب دیات الاعضاء ص ۲۷۸ نمبر ۴۵۵۶ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی دینۃ الاصابع ص نمبر ۱۳۹۱ / نسائی شریف ، نمبر ۴۸۵۷) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر انگلی میں دس اونٹ ہیں۔ اس لئے پانچ انگلیوں میں پچاس اونٹ لازم ہوں گے۔ اور تھیلی تک ہاتھ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ ان عمر قضى فى الابهام والتي تليها نصف الكف وفى الوسطى بعشر فرائض (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی هیته ۳۸ کم فی الاصابع جامس ص ۳۶۸ نمبر ۲۶۹۹۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہتھیلی تک ہاتھ ہے۔ اس لئے ہتھیلی تک کاٹے گا تو پچاس اونٹ نہیں لازم ہوں گئے۔
And for the fingers of the hand, half the diya. Then if he cuts them with the palm, then in it half the diya. All the fingers of the hand have half the diya. So if he cuts them including the palm, still half the diya. Each hand has five fingers, and the diya for each finger is ten camels. So the diya for five fingers is fifty camels. And fifty camels is the diya for one hand. Therefore, the diya for all five fingers is fifty camels, and fifty camels is the diya for one hand. So if he cuts all five fingers including the palm, still half the diya is necessary. The palm is considered part of the hand, and the diya for the hand is fifty camels, so if he cuts up to the palm, half the full diya (fifty camels) is due. (2) In the hadith: from Abu Musa from the Prophet (ﷺ), he said: 'The fingers are equal, ten camels each' (Abu Dawud no. 4556, Tirmidhi no. 1391, Nasa'i no. 4857). From this it is known that each finger has ten camels. Therefore, for five fingers, fifty camels are due. And the palm is part of the hand, as evidenced by the athar: 'Umar judged that the thumb and the next finger have half the diya of the palm, and the middle finger has ten fara'id (fractions)' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). From this athar, it is known that the palm is part of the hand, so cutting up to the palm entails fifty camels.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for the diya of the fingers of one hand. The diya for all five fingers of one hand is half of the full diya (50 camels). This is the same whether the fingers are cut alone or with the palm (the palm is considered part of the hand). The proof is from the hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari that each finger carries 10 camels, so five fingers make 50 camels. Additionally, an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab indicates that the palm is included in the hand, so cutting the palm does not add an extra amount beyond the 50 camels for the whole hand. The commentary explains that the full diya is 100 camels, so half is 50. The Hanafi position is that the diya for fingers is fixed per finger, but for the whole hand, it is half the diya, and cutting the palm does not increase it because the hand (including palm) is considered a single unit for diya purposes. Note that there is a nuance: if the fingers are cut with part of the forearm, then there is additional compensation (hukuma) for the forearm part, as per the next lesson.

Key Terms
اصابع اليد (asabi' al-yad): The five fingers of one hand (thumb, index, middle, ring, little).
الكف (al-kaff): The palm of the hand, which is considered part of the hand, so its diya is included in the hand's diya.

Key Takeaway

Diya for Hand and Forearm: Fixed vs. Discretionary
Ruling on diya when fingers are cut with half the forearm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diya when the hand is cut with part of the forearm, and apply the distinction between fixed diya (for the hand) and hukuma (for the forearm).

Core Idea
The hand has a fixed half-diya; the forearm requires hukuma because no fixed text exists.

In the Hanafi school, the diya for the hand (from fingertips to wrist joint) is fixed at half the full diya based on prophetic hadith. But when the cut extends into the forearm, the additional part has no explicit textual amount. This lesson examines how the Hanafi jurists resolve this through hukuma (judicial assessment), ensuring that all injuries receive just compensation even when no fixed amount is prescribed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is cutting the fingers along with half the forearm. The ruling: for the hand (palm) up to the wrist joint, half the diya (50 camels) is wajib. For the additional part (forearm), the judge determines hukuma.
The hand is defined as the part from fingertips to wrist joint.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith fixing diya for the hand and fingers, and athar from Ibrahim and Umar. The fixed amount ends at the wrist; beyond that, there is no nas, so hukuma applies based on general principles of justice.
Hadith is zanni al-thubut; hukuma is derived by qiyas and istihsan.
3
Understand the Hanafi definition of the hand
The Hanafi school considers the hand to be from the fingertips to the wrist joint. Cutting at the wrist triggers the fixed half-diya. Cutting above the wrist means the hand is partially severed, so the fixed amount applies only to the hand part.
This definition is based on the anatomical joint where the hand ends.
4
Apply to the case: fingers cut with forearm
If the cut goes through the palm and into the forearm, the hand part (palm with fingers) is still subject to half-diya because the hand is taken as a unit. The forearm part is a separate injury requiring hukuma.
The hukuma is assessed by the judge based on the severity of the loss.
5
Explain hukuma and its basis
Hukuma is an amount determined by the judge (hakim) for injuries without fixed diya. It is not arbitrary but based on proportionality to the full diya, considering the amount of flesh, bone, and disability caused.
Hukuma is a wajib obligation, but its quantum is discretionary.

۲۳۶۱ (۲۵) وان قطعها مع نصف الساعد ففى الكف نصف الدية وفي الزيادة حكومة
اگر انگلیوں کو آدھی کلائی تک کا ٹا تو ہتھیلی تک میں آدھی دیت اور اس سے زیادہ میں حاکم کا فیصلہ۔
انگلیوں سمیت آدھی تھیلی تک کا نا تو اس میں آدھی دیت لازم ہوگی اور تھیلی کے بعد کلائی تک جو کا ٹا اس میں حاکم کا جو فیصلہ کرے گا وہ لازم ہوگا۔
او پر اثر گزرا کہ ہتھیلی تک ہاتھ ہے اس لئے وہاں تک کہ لئے آدھی دیت ہوگی اور اس سے اوپر کلائی تک کہ لئے کچھ نہیں ہوا لیکن وہ بھی ہاتھ کا حصہ ہے اس لئے حاکم جتنی رقم کا فیصلہ کرے وہ لازم ہوگی (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال اذا قطعت الكف من المفصل قال حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت مجاہد نے فرمایا جا ئفہ زخم میں تہائی دیت ہے اور آر پار ہو جائے تو دو تہائی دیت ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا سب انگلیاں برابر ہیں دس دس اونٹ لازم ہوں گے (ج) حضرت عمر نے فیصلہ فرمایا انگوٹھا اور اس سے جوٹی ہوئی ہے تھیلی کی آدھی دیت ہے۔ اور بیچ کی انگلی میں پوری دیت کا دسواں حصہ دیت ہے یعنی دس اونٹ ۔
And if he cuts them with half the forearm, then for the palm half the diya, and for the excess (the part beyond the palm) hukuma (arbitrary compensation by the judge). If he cuts the fingers with half the forearm, then for the palm (the part up to the wrist?) there is half the diya, and for the excess (the additional part of the forearm) there is hukuma. If he cuts the fingers including half the palm, then half the diya becomes necessary, and for the part from the palm to the forearm, whatever the judge decides will be necessary. The athar passed that the hand extends to the palm, so for that part half the diya is due; for the part above up to the forearm, nothing is fixed, but since it is also a part of the body, the judge will assess an amount. (2) There is an athar from Ibrahim: when the hand is cut from the joint... Footnote: (a) Mujahid said: in the ja'ifah wound, one-third diya; if it penetrates, two-thirds. (b) He (the Prophet) said: all fingers are equal, ten camels each. (c) Umar judged: the thumb and the next finger have half the diya of the palm, and the middle finger has one-tenth of the full diya (ten camels).
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling when a person's fingers are cut along with half of the forearm (zā'idah, i.e., the additional part beyond the palm). The ruling is that for the palm (including fingers), half the diya (50 camels) is due because the hand (from fingertips to wrist joint) is considered one unit with a fixed diya of half the full diya. For the extra part (the forearm above the wrist), there is no fixed diya in the hadith, so the judge (hakim) determines an appropriate compensation (hukuma) based on the amount of flesh and bone lost. The commentary explains that the hand is defined as up to the palm (the wrist joint), so cutting at the wrist gives half diya. Cutting above that into the forearm means the fixed diya for the hand covers only the hand part; the forearm part is an additional loss that requires assessment. The hashiya includes a report from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and from Umar about specific finger diyas, which corroborate the fixed amounts. The footnote also repeats earlier rulings on ja'ifah and fingers. The authority weight is from the general principles of diyat; the hukuma is based on qiyas and istihsan.

Key Terms
حكومة (hukuma): An amount of compensation determined by the judge (hakim) for an injury that does not have a fixed diya in the Shariah, usually proportionate to the severity.
الزيادة (al-ziyadah): The additional part beyond the palm, i.e., the forearm (sā'id) when cut with the hand.
الكف (al-kaff): The hand from the wrist joint to the fingertips, including the palm and fingers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone cuts off the victim's hand at the middle of the forearm, what is the diya for the forearm part?
A) Half the diya
B) One-third diya
C) Hukuma (judge's assessment)
D) No diya

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi diyat law, the hand has a fixed half-diya, but any part above the wrist joint requires hukuma because it lacks explicit textual determination.

Diyat — Blood Money
beginner
6 min
Half Diyah for Fingers and Palm
Ruling on diyah for fingers and palm when cut together

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah for all five fingers of one hand according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Half diyah for the fingers of one hand: each finger is ten camels, total fifty.

This lesson presents the clear Hanafi ruling on diyah for the fingers of the hand. The matn states that for the fingers of the hand, half the diyah is due. The commentary explains that each hand has five fingers, and each finger's diyah is ten camels according to the hadith of Abu Musa. Thus five fingers total fifty camels, which is exactly half of the full diyah of a hand (100 camels). The ruling also applies if the cut includes the palm, because the palm is considered part of the hand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the body part and ruling level
The passage rules on the fingers of one hand. The diyah is wajib (obligatory financial compensation) for the loss of all five fingers.
Diyah is not fard because it is a civil liability.
2
Note the basis: fingers are half of hand diyah
The full diyah for a hand is 100 camels. The fingers constitute half of that, so 50 camels.
3
Understand the per-finger rate from hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The fingers are equal, ten camels each.' So each finger is 10 camels; five fingers = 50 camels.
The hadith is the primary evidence.
4
Confirm the inclusion of the palm
The commentary cites an athar from Umar that the palm is part of the hand. Therefore, cutting fingers with the palm still incurs only the diyah for the fingers (50 camels), not more.
The palm alone does not increase the diyah beyond the fingers.
5
Apply to scenario
Whether the cut is limited to fingers or includes the palm, the diyah is the same: 50 camels (half diyah of one hand).
If the entire hand (up to wrist) is cut, the diyah becomes full 100 camels.

وفى اصابع اليد نصف الدية فان قطعها مع الكف ففيها نصف الدية
ہاتھ کی ساری انگلیوں میں آدھی دیت ہے۔ پس اگر اس کو تھیلی سمیت کا نا تو بھی آدھی دیت ہے۔ ہر ہاتھ میں پانچ انگلیاں ہوتی ہیں اور ہر انگلی کی دیت دس اونٹ ہے۔ اس لئے پانچ انگلیوں کی دیت پچاس اونٹ ہوئے۔ اور پچاس اونٹ ایک ہاتھ کی دیت ہے۔ اس لئے ہاتھ کی پانچ انگلیوں کی دیت پچاس اونٹ ہوئے اور پچاس اونٹ ایک ہاتھ کی دیت ہے۔ اس لئے ہاتھ کی پانچوں انگلیوں کو تھیلی سمیت کا نا تب بھی آدھی دیت لازم ہوگی۔ ہتھیلی تک ہاتھ شمار ہوتا ہے اور ہاتھ کی دیت پچاس اونٹ ہے اس لئے ہتھیلی تک کاٹے گا تب بھی پوری دیت کی آدھی یعنی پچاس اونٹ لازم ہوں گے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی موسى عن النبي الا الله قال الاصابع سواء عشر عشر من الابل (ب)(ابوداؤد شریف، باب دیات الاعضاء ص ۲۷۸ نمبر ۴۵۵۶ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی دینۃ الاصابع ص نمبر ۱۳۹۱ / نسائی شریف ، نمبر ۴۸۵۷) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر انگلی میں دس اونٹ ہیں۔ اس لئے پانچ انگلیوں میں پچاس اونٹ لازم ہوں گے۔ اور تھیلی تک ہاتھ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ ان عمر قضى فى الابهام والتي تليها نصف الكف وفى الوسطى بعشر فرائض (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی هیته ۳۸ کم فی الاصابع جامس ص ۳۶۸ نمبر ۲۶۹۹۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہتھیلی تک ہاتھ ہے۔ اس لئے ہتھیلی تک کاٹے گا تو پچاس اونٹ نہیں لازم ہوں گئے۔
And for fingers of the hand, half the diyah. So if he cuts them with the palm, then half the diyah is due.
The diyah for all the fingers of the hand is half the diyah. So if he cuts them with the palm, still half the diyah is due. Each hand has five fingers, and the diyah for each finger is ten camels. Therefore the diyah for five fingers is fifty camels. And fifty camels is the diyah for one hand. Therefore the diyah for the five fingers of the hand is fifty camels, and fifty camels is the diyah for one hand. Therefore if he cuts all five fingers with the palm, still half the diyah is obligatory. The palm is considered part of the hand, and the diyah for the hand is fifty camels, so if he cuts up to the palm, still fifty camels are obligatory. (2) There is a hadith: From Abi Musa from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The fingers are equal, ten camels each.' From this it is known that each finger is ten camels. Therefore for five fingers, fifty camels are obligatory. And the palm is the hand as evidenced by the athar: 'Umar judged regarding the thumb and the one next to it half of the palm, and for the middle finger ten shares.' From this athar it is known that the palm is the hand. Therefore if he cuts up to the palm, fifty camels are not obligatory.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling on diyah for the fingers of the hand. The matn states that for the fingers of the hand, half the diyah is due. The commentary explains that each hand has five fingers, and each finger's diyah is ten camels according to the hadith of Abu Musa. Thus five fingers total fifty camels, which is exactly half of the full diyah of a hand (100 camels). The ruling also applies if the cut includes the palm, because the palm is considered part of the hand. The commentary cites the practice of Umar to confirm that the palm is part of the hand. Therefore, cutting the fingers with the palm still incurs the half diyah of fifty camels.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Financial compensation paid to the victim or his heirs for bodily injury or homicide.
اصابع (asabi'): Fingers, including thumb and others.
كف (kaff): Palm of the hand, considered part of the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the diyah for all five fingers of one hand if they are cut together with the palm?
A) One hundred camels
B) Fifty camels
C) Eighty camels
D) Twenty camels

Key Takeaway
The diyah for all five fingers of one hand is half the full diyah (50 camels), regardless of whether the palm is also cut, because the fingers constitute half the hand.
